  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12322186725632148702">Seventeen-year-old Alice and her mother have spent most of Alice’s life on the road, always a step ahead of the uncanny bad luck biting at their heels.   <span id="freeText12322186725632148702" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Alice and her mother have spent most of Alice’s life on the road, always a step ahead of the uncanny bad luck biting at their heels. But when Alice’s grandmother, the reclusive author of a cult-classic book of pitch-dark fairy tales, dies alone on her estate, the Hazel Wood, Alice learns how bad her luck can really get: her mother is stolen away-by a figure who claims to come from the Hinterland, the cruel supernatural world where her grandmother's stories are set. Alice's only lead is the message her mother left behind: “Stay away from the Hazel Wood.”<br /><br />Alice has long steered clear of her grandmother’s cultish fans. But now she has no choice but to ally with classmate Ellery Finch, a Hinterland superfan who may have his own reasons for wanting to help her. To retrieve her mother, Alice must venture first to the Hazel Wood, then into the world where her grandmother's tales began―and where she might find out how her own story went so wrong.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hello, and thank you! The book was inspired by my obsession with classic portal fantasy, fairy tales, and contemporary-set fantasies like The Magician<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hello, and thank you! The book was inspired by my obsession with classic portal fantasy, fairy tales, and contemporary-set fantasies like The Magicians; by an image I had in my head of a fairy-tale character breaking into the real world; and by my infatuation with general spec-fic weirdness: doors to the unknown, books that might be cursed, stories that live and breathe...<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_2026806837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026806837" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2026806837?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026806837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1977307337862447517">It's time for another <b>unpopular opinion</b> review! This book was literally the single biggest reading disappointment of the year for me. I really wanted to love this story. It was being marketed as a twisted fairytale, and those are my aesthetic for sure - the spookier and darker, the better - but this fell short in so many ways. <b>Please remember that these are just my opinions! You are more than welcome to disagree or tell me your thoughts, but please do so respectfully. ❤</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I wanted that distance</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1977307337862447517" style="display:none">It's time for another <b>unpopular opinion</b> review! This book was literally the single biggest reading disappointment of the year for me. I really wanted to love this story. It was being marketed as a twisted fairytale, and those are my aesthetic for sure - the spookier and darker, the better - but this fell short in so many ways. <b>Please remember that these are just my opinions! You are more than welcome to disagree or tell me your thoughts, but please do so respectfully. ❤</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I wanted that distance. I wanted that uncaring, 'here's your blood and guts and your fucked-up happy ending' fairy-tale voice."</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>genre marketing &amp; writing</i>
</b> ←<br />Marketing led me to believe that this was going to be the typical high fantasy world we see in fairytales. My first disappointment was in learning that the setting was modern-day New York, and the first half of the book straddled the line between contemporary and urban fantasy, at best.<br /><br />The story doesn't pick up as an actual <i>fantasy</i> tale until after the halfway mark, and when it does, the writing immediately becomes much less enjoyable. Anyone who knows my reading tastes knows I love flowery prose, but many of the descriptions in the fantasy "half" of this book go far past flowery, straight through whimsical, and land smack-dab in nonsense.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I did get it, I did. And the shame of it boiled into something darker. Before my brain could catch up, I jerked the wheel and turned the car off the road, sending us rattling toward the trees.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>Alice</i>
</b> ←<br />Let me put it this way: <i>The Hazel Wood</i> is my 200th read of 2017, and there have only been two narrators out of the entire other 199 titles that held a candle to how terrible Alice is. She starts the book off poorly, rambling about her anger issues without giving us any reason as to <i>why</i> she's talking about them. As it progresses, <b>she expresses actual, unwarranted physical violence</b> towards other characters (including attempting to kill them via vehicular manslaughter because she feels guilty for her own poor choices).<br /><br />She shouts and snaps constantly, has no respect for anyone (besides her mother), and judges everyone she meets hyper-critically. Her judgmental nature even borders on <b>ableism</b> when she meets a character who has been driven to a broken mental state by entering the Hazel Wood: Alice has several internal monologues about how little she trusts the woman's hygiene and the state of the woman's home's cleanliness, solely because she doesn't deem the woman "sane enough".<br /><br />Even when she enlists the help of Finch, she is incessantly rude, critical, and offensive towards him. When she is <b>finally</b> called out on her offensive nature, she deflects, makes excuses, and has a general disregard for any harm she has caused. In one scenario, when he remarks on her misogynistic speech, her actual comeback is, <i>"Oh, my god, Finch, go get a liberal arts degree"</i> (I read this three times in hopes of making sense of it before deciding that she learned her snark from old men in facebook comment threads).<br /><br />Beyond all of the ways in which Alice's character is incredibly harmful and is rarely - if ever - challenged for most of her behaviors, she's also just not well-written. She's hypocritical, self-contradicting, and outright <i>
  <b>boring.</b>
</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Maybe Finch wasn't trying to be the sidekick in my story. Maybe he was trying to start one of his own.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>Finch</i>
</b> ←<br />Finch is introduced in a way that gave me actual optimism for the story: he's a classmate of hers who is kind and welcoming, seeks her friendship, and offers to face certain danger to help her find the Hazel Wood and her mother. Unfortunately, my optimism started to falter when I learned that Finch, the <b>single</b> black character in the story (in New York City, no less), is commented on multiple times as being unattractive and "a waste of wealth" - never challenged.<br /><br />That was the first red flag - in a book with no commentary on anyone else's features, the <i>single</i> person of color is the only unattractive one? - but it worsens when Finch, despite being a very present figure throughout the story, is never fleshed out. He feels incredibly one-dimensional from start to finish, though some of this may just be to blame on Alice's refusal to let him speak for more than thirty seconds without telling him to shut up.<br /><br />It felt like there was some small attempt to have a dialogue on racism and privilege when Finch talks to Alice about being afraid of racial profiling, but it's thrown away when Alice immediately insinuates that his father's wealth negates any racism he faces, and then further derails the conversation every time he tries to speak to her about it. By the end of the book, I resigned myself to the feeling that Finch was, in every shape and form, a Token Black Character™. His entire character arc felt so <i>bad</i> to read.<br /><br />→ <b>
  <i>fairytales</i>
</b> ←<br />Literally the only redeeming aspect of this book, for me, was the occasional time when we would get to hear one of Althea's tales. Sadly, they're incredibly few and far between - I think we only got two full tales in the entire book. I enjoyed those stories, and would probably read a bind-up of them, but within the context of the entire book, they weren't enough to salvage it.<br /><br />→ <b>
  <i>FINAL THOUGHTS</i>
</b> ←<br />This book was just a total disaster from start to finish for me, and the only reason I didn't DNF it at the 40% mark was because I was so desperately hoping it would improve by the end. I would more than likely not pick up any future books by Melissa Albert, and cannot, in good faith, recommend this story to anyone.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Flatiron for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/12/22/the-hazel-wood/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> on my blog!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1977307337862447517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2143599525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143599525" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143599525?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143599525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8428045600831510944"><blockquote>
  <i>Did her insides match her outsides? Was the way my life dripped off me like water, barely leaving a mark, normal?</i>
</blockquote><br/>Okay, so this was <u>not</u> a book for me. I really wish I hadn’t received an arc of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34275232.The_Hazel_Wood__The_Hazel_Wood___1_' title='The Hazel Wood (The Hazel Wood, #1) by Melissa Albert' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hazel Wood</a> and had instead waited for more reviews to roll in first. <br/><br/>The blurb makes it sound exactly like the kind of dark fairy tale goodness I love, but if someone had - more accurately - explained that this is a book about a girl called Alice who gets sent to <s>Wonderland</s> the Hinterland where she </span>
  <span id="freeText8428045600831510944" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Did her insides match her outsides? Was the way my life dripped off me like water, barely leaving a mark, normal?</i>
</blockquote><br />Okay, so this was <u>not</u> a book for me. I really wish I hadn’t received an arc of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34275232.The_Hazel_Wood__The_Hazel_Wood___1_" title="The Hazel Wood (The Hazel Wood, #1) by Melissa Albert" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hazel Wood</a> and had instead waited for more reviews to roll in first. <br /><br />The blurb makes it sound exactly like the kind of dark fairy tale goodness I love, but if someone had - more accurately - explained that this is a book about a girl called Alice who gets sent to <s>Wonderland</s> the Hinterland where she meets <s>tweedle dee and tweedle dum</s> many colourful characters who talk in riddles, and she finds herself doing bizarre and random things like <s>attending an unbirthday party</s> singing “Smells Like Teen Spirit” and “Landslide” in a Tudor-style pub… well, I’d have passed. I’ve already read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24213.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___Through_the_Looking_Glass" title="Alice's Adventures in Wonderland &amp; Through the Looking-Glass by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a>. Once was enough.<br /><br />I know this will be much more suited to a specific type of reader who likes <b>dreamy, nonsensical prose, heavy on the metaphors</b>. Perhaps those who enjoyed books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27883214.Caraval__Caraval___1_" title="Caraval (Caraval, #1) by Stephanie Garber" rel="nofollow noopener">Caraval</a>. Those who are more forgiving of no one saying what they actually mean and talking all mysterious for no other reason than “shh, this is the rule of fairytales” because we all know it's more magical if nothing makes sense. For me, it was honestly irritating to have characters withhold important information just ‘cause.<br /><br />The book opens with a bit of background about Alice, her mother Ella, and her reclusive grandmother Althea Proserpine - an author of a dark fairy tale collection, <i>Tales from the Hinterland</i>, that gained a cult following some years back. Alice has never met her grandmother, but Ella has constantly insisted on the two of them packing up and moving again and again, running away from bad luck that clearly has something to do with her grandmother and the book she wrote.<br /><br />When Ella disappears, seemingly kidnapped, Alice teams up with long-time Althea fan, Ellery Finch, and uses his knowledge of the stories to find her grandmother's secret estate - The Hazel Wood.<br /><br />This first half(ish) seemed <b>very slow and longer than necessary.</b> It is mostly a road trip where the characters rely on fairy tale logic along the lines of <i>if it wants you to find it, you will</i> instead of smarts and deduction to keep the story moving. A romance develops but, to the author's credit, she never allows this to become a romantic book overall.<br /><br />I found a lot of the story really hard to get through. Maybe because I struggled to form a connection with any character. Alice herself is cold and bitchy, without the depth and complexity needed to make these traits interesting. Ellery Finch is super hipster and must gaze at the moon and quote Shakespeare every few pages in order to keep functioning. He has a tattoo of a Vonnegut quote, of course. And the problem is these two are the only really valuable or memorable characters in the book.<br /><br />The second half basically is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24213.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___Through_the_Looking_Glass" title="Alice's Adventures in Wonderland &amp; Through the Looking-Glass by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a>. Which may or may not sound appealing, but my tolerance level for random weirdness isn't that high.<br /><br />My favourite parts were the <i>Tales from the Hinterland</i> fairy tales within the story, which were deliciously dark and creepy, but I disliked it every time we came back to "reality" with Alice and Finch. I kinda wish the author had written a book of short stories instead and let me skip out on everything else. I could definitely see myself enjoying a creepy short story collection from Albert.<br /><br />So, yeah, definitely not for me, but I would recommend this for those who like Wonderland retellings, and those who enjoy really lyrical prose over characters and/or plot.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8428045600831510944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=subscription-box-owlcrate">subscription-box-owlcrate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=subscription-box-fairyloot">subscription-box-fairyloot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127729110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17566313044394073773"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508123315i/24183647._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Flatiron Books in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Once upon a time there was a beautiful queen who thought words were stronger than anything. She used them to win love and money and gifts. She used them to carry her across the world.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Let me just start this off by saying that I normally only one star something if it has very problematic content. This book only has one element that made me uncomfortable (that I will talk about later on), but the main reason I’m giving th</span>
  <span id="freeText17566313044394073773" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508123315i/24183647._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Flatiron Books in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Once upon a time there was a beautiful queen who thought words were stronger than anything. She used them to win love and money and gifts. She used them to carry her across the world.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Let me just start this off by saying that I normally only one star something if it has very problematic content. This book only has one element that made me uncomfortable (that I will talk about later on), but the main reason I’m giving this one star is because it was so ungodly boring. <br><br>Next, and this could be completely my fault, I feel like this is marketed as a YA Fantasy, when it takes the reader almost 250 pages, out of a 360 page book, to even get into the fantasy aspect and by that time I couldn't care less about some pseudo <i>Alice in Wonderland</i>. This reads like a YA Contemporary Mystery and that is not a genre that I enjoy reading in the slightest, so maybe that is the main reason this didn’t work for me. <br><br>So the basic premise of <i>The Hazel Wood</i> is that a seventeen-year-old girl named Alice has been on the run with her mother, Ella, for as long as she can remember. They go from city to city, house to house, sometimes sleeping in their car, always on the run from the “bad luck” that follows them. Alice’s grandmother, Ella’s mother, is a very famous author who wrote a collection of short stories that are incredibly hard to find in today’s world. The short stories are very dark fairytales, that have netted her grandmother a very cult-like fanbase that totally gave me some <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1486484641" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfilm</a> vibes if I’m being completely honest. <br><br>Alice has never met her grandmother, and she’s never visited the exclusive estate she lives on called the Hazel Wood. But after Alice’s mother is kidnapped, she is desperate to find any means possible to finally visit the mysterious estate and to get her mother back once and for all. <br><br>But this book was so incredibly slow. I had to bribe myself with chocolates to even finish it. This is a 360 page book, and it took me SEVENTEEN days to read it. That’s a little over 20 pages a day. And that’s honestly all I could do, because I was so uninvested. And it’s actually mindboggling to me that this book is even 360 pages long, because I feel like everything could have taken place in 150-200 pages, too. <br><br>And Alice is such an unlikeable main character that isn’t supposed to be an unlikeable main character. She’s so rude, and self-centered, and unable to recognize her privilege because she can’t get over the fact that she grew up poor. She talks over people, and is demanding, and refuses to acknowledge her mistakes. I could never and will never connect with her, and it was honestly miserable to be inside of her head.<br><br>So, the problematic element is the treatment of the biracial side character who Alice spends most of the book with. Finch is the only person of color in this book, and Alice constantly remarks on how unattractive he is, and it feels really bad. Then, when they get into an altercation with a police officer, Finch tries to explain to Alice about racial profiling and how he feels uncomfortable being around cops and being noncompliant around cops, while Alice just completely disregards his very valid feelings by saying he’s rich and privileged. Like that negates the color of his skin and the racism he faces every single day because of it, because she grew up poor and on the run with her mom. On top of the fact that Alice will never let Finch speak, because she’s always interrupting and talking over him. It just reads badly and made my very uncomfortable while reading. Also, Alice even got physically abusive a couple times and I just wasn't there for it at all. <br><br>The other minor thing that just made me feel a little uncomfortable while reading was that this book kind of romanticizes kidnapping. Like, Alice has very fond memories of being kidnapped when she was six and it feels almost like glorifying it. Maybe this just rubbed me the wrong way because I was always deathly afraid of being kidnapped as a child, but I didn’t enjoy reading her memories on kidnapping whatsoever, either.<br><br>And the last thing is that the deus ex machina in this book is very strong. So many things just so conveniently happened, especially at the end of this book when we are finally in a fairytale land, to wrap up this story. <br><br>The only thing I truly liked about this book were the two chapters that were stories that Finch was retelling to Alice from inside her Grandmother’s book, <i> Tales from the Hinterland</i>. Both of these were honestly great, and I enjoyed them immensely and it showcased that the author does have talent for writing. Unfortunately, this is only two chapters of a thirty-one chapter book. But both of those short stories were good and I enjoyed each one more than the rest of this entire book combined<br><br>Also, have you seen the finished copy of this? With its foil sprayed pages? Holy moly, it’s honestly one of the most beautiful books I’ve ever laid eyes upon. But you all know what they say about judging books by their covers…<br><br>This book just wasn’t for me or my tastes. We aren’t even in 2018 yet and I can tell you that this will 100% make my most disappointing publications of 2018 list. And from all my friends’ reviews, I truly think this is going to just be a polarizing book! People are going to hate and dread picking it up, or they are going to be completely engrossed, love, and devour it. And you guys know that just because I disliked this book, it doesn’t mean that your feelings are invalid. If you liked this book then I am truly happy for you, but this book just really didn’t work for me. And if you do decide to pick this one up, I hope you find way more enjoyment within its pages than I did. <br><br>Content warnings for underage alcohol consumption, drug use, self-harm, talk of suicide, and mild violence. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><i>The quote above was taken from an ARC and is subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7695806-bitchin-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenn</a>! ❤<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519852046i/25139815._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This was in the February 2018 <a href="https://owlcrate.com/refer/Hersh-FUXKTCQE" rel="nofollow noopener">OwlCrate</a> box!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17566313044394073773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2320751541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320751541" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320751541?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320751541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10041917794192974130">3 Stars. Not my favorite book I’ve ever read, but still enjoyable.<br/><br/>I don’t have particularly strong feelings about this book. The writing was fine. The characters were okay. The world was probably the most interesting element of the story, but nothing amazing in my opinion. I really enjoyed how the story takes place in modern day New York City and the fairytale elements are hidden beneath. I found the fairytales/whimsical elements of the story to be it’s strongest point. I genuinely enjoyed my ti</span>
  <span id="freeText10041917794192974130" style="display:none">3 Stars. Not my favorite book I’ve ever read, but still enjoyable.<br /><br />I don’t have particularly strong feelings about this book. The writing was fine. The characters were okay. The world was probably the most interesting element of the story, but nothing amazing in my opinion. I really enjoyed how the story takes place in modern day New York City and the fairytale elements are hidden beneath. I found the fairytales/whimsical elements of the story to be it’s strongest point. I genuinely enjoyed my time listening to this story on audiobook, but I don’t feel it has many incredible aspects. Additionally, I did lose focus nearing the end of the story. Stories became jumbled and it left me feeling as if the ending has less impact than it intended to.<br /><br />I find one of the biggest critiques of this novel is that the main character, Alice, is immensely rude, disrespectful, hyper-critical and ill-tempered which is <b>100% true</b>. That being said, her personality/behavior is integral to the story and does have a purpose, so it didn’t bother me all that much. Given, every time Alice made an effort to point out her “rage issues”, I totally rolled my eyes, but it didn’t make me significantly more frustrated than other unlikeable main characters. I understand the valid criticisms of how Alice treats the only person of color in the story because that was a bit more off-putting than her other traits. There is a scene where Finch, a biracial character, tries to calmly explain why Alice provoking a police officer in his company can be dangerous and Alice completely brushes off his concerns, trivializing the racism he experiences because he comes from money. (It was obvious to me that this scene was intended to be a lesson in privilege and we were meant to side with Finch, but as it is from Alice’s perspective and there is no correction of her behavior on her part, her voice is more dominant so I can completely see the flaws in execution of this scene. It was just messy.) I will also mention that I actually enjoyed the fact that this story followed a main character who grew up in poverty and without a stable home – Situations like this are not common in YA and it was nice to see a character who constantly moved from place to place, have been kicked out by people they stay with, always on the road and have a parent who is always working odd jobs to make ends meet. Alice isn’t the worst main character I’ve ever read about (though she’s pretty close to the bottom), but I don’t feel much affection for her. Finch was by far my favorite character in the story (though there aren’t many others to choose from) and I really wish he had gotten more development instead of being constantly pushed off to the side. He had great potential, but it didn’t really follow through.<br /><br />I did enjoy <i>The Hazel Wood</i> but it’s not a very memorable book for me. I think the synopsis was so strong and there was so many possibilities for this book to be amazing, but I don’t think it followed the strongest route. It’s just one of those books that I didn’t love or hate either, that I had a good time reading, but have more distinct critiques than positives to share.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10041917794192974130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2092612632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2092612632" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2092612632?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/40656322-flatiron-books">Flatiron Books</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2092612632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6900262877080609612"><i>"Everything was beautiful, and nothing hurt."</i><br/><br/>You know those Disney princess fairytales, the ones where the damsel in distress is saved by Prince Charming and they get married and live happily ever after? Yeah, this isn't that story. Think of the old school <i>Brother's Grimm</i> fairytales, and then imagine something even darker and you'll have a clear picture of what this book holds for you. That's not a criticism; one of the surest ways to get me to commit to reading a book is to tell me it's an old </span>
  <span id="freeText6900262877080609612" style="display:none"><i>"Everything was beautiful, and nothing hurt."</i><br /><br />You know those Disney princess fairytales, the ones where the damsel in distress is saved by Prince Charming and they get married and live happily ever after? Yeah, this isn't that story. Think of the old school <i>Brother's Grimm</i> fairytales, and then imagine something even darker and you'll have a clear picture of what this book holds for you. That's not a criticism; one of the surest ways to get me to commit to reading a book is to tell me it's an old school fairytale. I am a hardcore sucker for these wicked little snippets into an alternate world, and this debut felt like it was written by a seasoned pro with all the bells and whistles you could ask for. <br /><br /><i>When Alice was born, her eyes were black from end to end, and the midwife didn't stay long enough to wash her.</i><br /><br />We're dropped into the story about midway; the first few chapters are meant to give us some background on Alice, her mother Ella, and her grandmother Althea Prosperine, who became famous by writing a book of fairytales. This book was titled <i>Tales From The Hinterland</i> and it contained a total of twelve brief stories. The cool part about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34275232.The_Hazel_Wood" title="The Hazel Wood by Melissa Albert" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hazel Wood</a> is that we get to read a couple of these first hand within the story (<i>Three Times Alice</i> and <i>The Door That Wasn't There</i>), while also getting brief snippets from most of the rest of them toward the end. This aspect was so unique and compelling that I felt a little breathless at the end. I wanted every story verbatim! I feel like, if the author so chose, she could write <i>Tales From The Hinterland</i>, binding and fully fleshing out all twelve stories in a volume to sell as a companion novel and we the people would EAT. IT. UP. <s>Seriously, please please pretty please?</s><br /><br />So Alice remembers being kidnapped at the age of six by a strange man with red hair claiming to take her to visit her recluse of a grandmother, but she was never harmed and never laid eyes on Althea. Strange things begin to happen, such as Alice spotting the mysterious redheaded man a decade after her last sighting of him, her mother and herself receiving a letter stating Althea has passed away, and finally, Ella disappearing under very strange circumstances. Alice has no one to turn to other than a recently made acquaintance named Ellery Finch, who is a mega super borderline stalker fan of Althea's work. His money and affluent nature allow them to forge a shaky bond and they decide to set off on a journey to do the very thing Alice's mother warned her not to do-visit the Hazel Wood. &lt;---<i>Name of Althea Prosperine's vast estate in upstate New York</i><br /><br /><i>I hated needing something from someone when I had absolutely nothing to offer back. You'd think, after the upbringing I'd had, I'd at least be used to it.</i><br /><br />I wouldn't call Alice a likable character, but she was certainly a compelling lead. I felt just as befuddled as she did along this journey; I honestly had no clue where this story would take us and was just as shocked as Alice at every twist and turn. While there was no sexual content whatsoever in this book (at least that I remember), it still made me give pause to what age range this book would be most appropriate for. Certainly the older side of the spectrum, as this was disturbing, unsettling, and contained a good bit of graphic violence/horror within the stories. I was warned many times over about how truly dark this book is, but I didn't think it was something I'd blink an eye at, not with all the graphic murder mystery/thrillers I read, but this was different. I can't quite put my finger on what exactly provoked this sense of unease I felt; perhaps it was the not so light way the story was wrapped up? There isn't much levity to be found here; if you're the type of reader looking for a happy ending you most certainly have come to the wrong place. <br /><br />Originally I gave this book 4 stars, but I've decided to bump it up to a full 5, seeing as it's been almost a full week since I finished it and I cannot stop thinking about it. This quirky little novel has been jostling other stories I am currently reading, vying for attention in my head and further pondering, so for that reason, I think I need to give credit where credit is due. This book certainly won't be for everyone, but I think the fans of dark fairytales and things that go bump in the night will wholly appreciate the author's ability to conjure up such a complex tale that was detailed and, quite frankly, brilliant. Highly recommended!<br /><br /><b>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my copy.</b><br /><br /><i>Book #4 in my Nebulous November challenge! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6900262877080609612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2400047854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2400047854" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2400047854?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2400047854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17003817378892725918"><i>
  <b>"And while they're being told, stories create the energy that makes this world go. They keep our stars in place. They make our grass grow." </b>
</i><br/><br/>You want to read a mysterious, crazily intriguing book, this is it. My heart was racing for the first 7 chapters because I had no idea what was going to happen and during the rest because I couldn’t wait to see where the Story was going (pun intended- if you’ve read it you’ll understand).<br/><br/>This is just so <i>AMAZING</i>. I don’t know how it possible to make somet</span>
  <span id="freeText17003817378892725918" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"And while they're being told, stories create the energy that makes this world go. They keep our stars in place. They make our grass grow." </b>
</i><br /><br />You want to read a mysterious, crazily intriguing book, this is it. My heart was racing for the first 7 chapters because I had no idea what was going to happen and during the rest because I couldn’t wait to see where the Story was going (pun intended- if you’ve read it you’ll understand).<br /><br />This is just so <i>AMAZING</i>. I don’t know how it possible to make something so interesting and addicting. I couldn’t stop even once, it’s crazy really, in the entire book not even one word was boring or out of place. I feel like I’m going to burst into hysterical laughter if I start talking about it because I can’t wait for the next book and I can’t accept the fact that the book is over. The whole thing was so well planned and the book did justice to the concept which was also great. The world itself is written very descriptively which helped picture the very fictional and fantastical world and characters. It was so much more interesting because nearly every other character had their own agenda and were playing their own angle.<br /><br />In this world, Althea Proserpine was a famous writer who wrote the books <i>Tales of Hinterland</i>. This book is an enigma, there are no traces of it online and very few people have read it and those who have read it are borderline addicted to it and Althea, Once this book was published Althea Proserpine moved into an estate called <i>The Hazel Wood</i> and fans all over the world have tried to locate it with no avail. And just like that Althea Proserpine was never again seen on the face of the Earth and eventually the theories and rumours died down, but Althea’s daughter Ella moved out of <i>The Hazel Wood</i> when she was young and raised her daughter Alice away from anything related to Althea and her fairytales and forbade her from researching or reaching out to Althea. <br /><br />But all her life Alice and her mother have been moving from place to place without ever settling down because if they ever stay in one place for too long bad luck just seems to follow them and bring a whole lot of destruction along with it. But a few years ago Alice got a letter informing her of Althea Proserpine’s death and at that moment onwards she built a stable life for herself and her daughter. But now Alice has been taken by someone who claims to be from Hinterland, the very world Althea based all her stories on, which now turns out to be real. And if the world is real so must be the stories.<br /><br />The fairytales Althea wrote were not our average fairy tales with happy endings, they were gruesome tales generally with savage endings and characters who held no semblance of humanity. Now that Hinterland has proved to be real Alice will have to have navigate a world of the darkest stories in existence to rescue her mother, with the help of Finch who happens to be one of her grandmothers cultish superfans who remembers every story in the book.<br /><br />This book grabbed my attention in the beginning and held it all the way to the end. The world within this world is one of the most interesting I have ever read. The concept of the Hinterland and the Hazel Wood was written with a lot of clarity which increases the pace of the book. Everything about this book dragged me in and the next book has a lot of intrigue to live up to. I rate this book 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17003817378892725918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3636706896233476434">this is the first book that has made me think that the author statements/praise on the back cover are completely made up. i mean, unless i have a defect copy, the fact that stephanie garber, karen mcmanus, seanan mcguire AND jennifer niven all adored this is highly suspicious, because this story is a hot mess.<br/><br/>reading this (the plot specifically) reminded me of every time i have to untangle my headphones - it only becomes more and more of a mess until i get so frustrated and i throw them across t</span>
  <span id="freeText3636706896233476434" style="display:none">this is the first book that has made me think that the author statements/praise on the back cover are completely made up. i mean, unless i have a defect copy, the fact that stephanie garber, karen mcmanus, seanan mcguire AND jennifer niven all adored this is highly suspicious, because this story is a hot mess.<br /><br />reading this (the plot specifically) reminded me of every time i have to untangle my headphones - it only becomes more and more of a mess until i get so frustrated and i throw them across the room. i thought that if i continued reading, the plot would become more clear and make sense, but instead it became more muddled and absurd. i also had issues with the lack of character development, inconsistent world building, and erratic pacing. <br /><br />overall, this is just a really poor execution of an unique, and what was a potentially interesting, story. such a shame. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>2.5 stars</i></b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251292743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15063281078819957840">Finally, I had an unpopular opinion………...but in the <i>fun</i> way!<br/><br/>Honestly, even though hating the books that everyone loves makes me feel #quirky and #unique and dare I say...not like other girls, it gets old. Hating the books your friends love = no fun. <br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/04/02/books-i-like-that-no-one-else-does-even-my-positive-opinions-are-unpopular/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>Liking the books your friends hate, on the other hand: A BLAST.<br/><br/>All the shenanigans and special-snowflake-ness of an unpopular opinion with none of the pain and full-on suffering of reading a bad book! I should </span>
  <span id="freeText15063281078819957840" style="display:none">Finally, I had an unpopular opinion………...but in the <i>fun</i> way!<br /><br />Honestly, even though hating the books that everyone loves makes me feel #quirky and #unique and dare I say...not like other girls, it gets old. Hating the books your friends love = no fun. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/04/02/books-i-like-that-no-one-else-does-even-my-positive-opinions-are-unpopular/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />Liking the books your friends hate, on the other hand: A BLAST.<br /><br />All the shenanigans and special-snowflake-ness of an unpopular opinion with none of the pain and full-on suffering of reading a bad book! I should do this more often. Fingers crossed.<br /><br />Now it’s time for the hard part of the review, when I have to explain why I liked the book. Which, in this case? Difficult.<br /><br />Synopsis first. Let’s put the hard stuff off. Procrastination nation and all that!!!<br /><br />Alice is a weirdo teenage girl who has been on the run with her mom, Ella, for her whole life. Not on the run from the law. As fun as that would be, this is EVEN MORE FUN: they are on the run from bad luck!!! Everywhere they go, bad luck follows them.<br /><br />Then Alice’s grandmother dies. Ol’ Granny was the author of a cult-classic book of creeeepy fairytales. Alice has long been obsessed with her, but never met her - and never read the book, although she’s read all the information on it she can find. Once Grandmama dies, Alice’s mom, who she constantly calls by her first name like the lil rebel she is, is hype. She’s like, bad luck over! We’re moving to the Big Apple, baby.<br /><br />And they do. Ella marries a reeeeaaaaally rich guy. Alice goes to a private school and works in an overpriced pretentious coffee shop. They’re living large.<br /><br />Until Ella gets kidnapped, and Alice is forced to do exactly what she was told NOT to do: Team up with one of Grandmummy’s crazy fans (her semi-attractive classmate, Ellery Finch) and go to G-ma’s estate (The Hazel Wood).<br /><br />I love fairytales, dark and creeeeepy ones most of all, so...pretty ideal for me. Yeah.<br /><br />Now, good news or bad news first? Let’s do bad news.<br /><br />Alice sucks.<br /><br />Yes, the main character of this whole shindig. We do indeed spend the lion’s share of our time in her head. It’s not a buttered-popcorn-flavored jellybean level of unpleasant, but it’s not awesome.<br /><br />Alice is very mean. Unnecessarily so. I am okay with a mean character sometimes, if they are also badass and/or smart, but Alice is not extremely either of those. It makes for a bumpy ride.<br /><br />She is really obsessed with her mom, too. Like, actually the only relationship in her life is with her mom. It’s pretty toxic stuff. Never corrected, because of course not, but there are more books. Fingers crossed.<br /><br />Alice sucks, and partner-in-crime extraordinaire Ellery Finch (who goes by his last name, as is the habit of the worst kinds of pretentious YA rich boys), is eh at best. So not off to a good start.<br /><br />The other characters (Alice’s stepfather and stepsister; Ella; people who hop in and out of the narrative as is convenient) are not awesome either.<br /><br />In most books, without-exception-sh*tty characters would be a dealbreaker. But not here, my dear boy! Au contraire, mon frère! They make up for it, almost, but not to the degree that I’d give it any more than 3.5 stars. <br /><br />As mentioned, I love fairytales, and this feels very fairytaley. Which is extremely rare in YA, I think. It’s a particular feeling. It’s also really creepy! How cool is that! Also so rare! This book is atmospheric as hell and it full-on nails it.<br /><br />I also lovelovelove the writing style. It is, as I literally just said, fairytaley/creepy/atmospheric. It is also beautiful, AND SO RICH IN DETAIL I COULD DIE OF HAPPINESS. I am obsessed with fun facts, but I don’t think those work super well outside of contemporary. <br /><br />So it’s cool that this book did one better: it just entwined lots of details and allusions and names and places and objects and books and people and artists into the text, and made me Google. I LOVED IT. I Googled so many things and read so many Wikipedia pages in the course of this book. What more could you want?<br /><br />It makes such a detailed, realistic world (v helpful for magical realism as bonkers as this) and is also just the best reading experience.<br /><br />Also. Also also also: NO ROMANCE.<br /><br />YES.<br /><br />YOU READ THAT CORRECTLY.<br /><br />NOOOOOOOOO ROMANCE WHATSOEVER.<br /><br />Okay, maybe traces. When you read “partnered up with semi-attractive boy of her own age,” or whatever equivalent phrase I wrote in my handy-dandy synopsis (yes, I am literally so lazy that I won’t scroll up in my own review, what of it) I’m sure you assumed “ah, there is the romance.”<br /><br />Me too, baby blue. (Look at me making up expressions. It’s almost like this is the seventh review in a row I’m writing.) Anyway. There are romancey moments between Finch and Alice. Alice almost-but-not-quite feels something for him. It might be friendship.<br /><br />Either way, they don’t end up together. (Spoiler?? I don’t know who cares! Does it count as a spoiler if it’s a good thing that should convince you to read the book?? Sorry if it does but also I disagree with you!) I don’t think they kiss either, unless I’ve forgotten a beautiful romantic moment between descriptions of pee-scented pillows. <br /><br />And a YA fantasy without a romance is more refreshing than I can say.<br /><br />Also, I want to read Tales from the Hinterland (Grandnanny’s book) so badly. If Melissa Albert is smart, or loves me or the world or both, she will write that spinoff.<br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b>: I’ve never read a YA fantasy book like this!!! And it wasn’t perfect but I’m going to chase that feeling of uniqueness baby!<br /><br /><br />------<br /><br />finally a reverse unpopular opinion!!! finally a book i like that none of my most trusted reviewers do!<br /><br />...<br /><br />is this supposed to teach me empathy? because i still feel fun and unique AND i had all the fun of liking a book.<br /><br />review to come!!<br /><br />------<br /><br /><br /><br />an interesting way to read a book is by assuming it's an alice's adventures in wonderland retelling just because the protagonist is named alice and then slowly realizing it has nothing to do with that at all<br /><br />but this is going swimmingly, considering</span>
  <a data-text-id="15063281078819957840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2059720983?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads">ELLIAS (elliasreads)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2059720983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12006574203549558168"><b>THREE THOUGHTS ABOUT THIS BOOK</b>.<br/><br/>1) I heard that this book had <i>The Raven Boys</i> vibes and I was sooo excited to read this book and find out more as to why it resembled one of my favorites series of all time <b>BUT</b>......<br/><br/>literally,<br/><br/><b>FUCKING LIESSSSSS. I SEE NOTHING, <i>N O T H I N G</i>, ABOUT THIS BOOK THAT RESEMBLES MY FAVORITE BABIES OF ALL TIME. TO EVEN COMPARE THE TWO IS SACRILEGIOUS WTF.</b> <br/><br/>People say,<br/><br/>"Oh, the writing!" <br/><b>NO</b>.<br/>"Oh, the atmosphere!"<br/><b>NO</b>.<br/>"Oh, the story!"<br/><b>HELL TO THE FUKCING NOPE</b>.<br/><br/>JUST NOPE. NOPE. NOPE. </span>
  <span id="freeText12006574203549558168" style="display:none"><b>THREE THOUGHTS ABOUT THIS BOOK</b>.<br /><br />1) I heard that this book had <i>The Raven Boys</i> vibes and I was sooo excited to read this book and find out more as to why it resembled one of my favorites series of all time <b>BUT</b>......<br /><br />literally,<br /><br /><b>FUCKING LIESSSSSS. I SEE NOTHING, <i>N O T H I N G</i>, ABOUT THIS BOOK THAT RESEMBLES MY FAVORITE BABIES OF ALL TIME. TO EVEN COMPARE THE TWO IS SACRILEGIOUS WTF.</b> <br /><br />People say,<br /><br />"Oh, the writing!" <br /><b>NO</b>.<br />"Oh, the atmosphere!"<br /><b>NO</b>.<br />"Oh, the story!"<br /><b>HELL TO THE FUKCING NOPE</b>.<br /><br />JUST NOPE. NOPE. NOPE. NOPE. <b>NOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO</b>. <br /><br />Holy fucking moly. <br /><br />2) People are comparing this to a'darker' tale mashup of 'Alice in Wonderland' buuttt this book really reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18770398.Night_Film" title="Night Film by Marisha Pessl" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Film</a>.. <br /><br />Why? <br /><br />Because literally there were so many parts of the book (last 2/3s) that vaguely did not make sense to me and even after rereading certain passages I just gave up. I just couldn't <u>grasp the full of <i><b>it</b></i></u>.<br /><br />It was so confusing; sure the writing was good and the premise of the story overall is actually <i>really</i> intriguing and unique....but I just couldn't grasp the finality of certain passages of scenes in the book???<br /><br />Or maybe I'm just too stupid to understand lmao. <br /><br />3) Alice, the main character.....my god so annoooyyyinnggg. She is an unlikable character made to be unlikable to be liked as a flawed character but I couldn't do it. She was so arrogant and selfish sometimes I just wanted to shout at her. Also the way she treated another person of color, a boy, was just plain ignorant and fucking stupid. They got stopped by a cop and he told her how he was uncomfortable around them and about his skin color and literally this white girl tells him to shut up and goes off about how he is super rich and has a ton of privilege....<br /><br />LIKE.....???? <br /><br />She was gonna run their car into a fucking tree because she got to pissed at <i>this</i> conversation and I was so fucking iritated I put the book down and drank a glass of water. <br /><br />Irrelevant but still.<br /><br />Alice, honey, grow the fuck up. <br /><br /><br />Literally this book was one of my most anticipated releases of 2018 and so far, two of my most anticipated reads have been let downs and now I'm just<u> flat out annoyed writing this stupid <i>review</i></u> and I was going to give this book three stars because it wasn't that bad but <b>NOT</b> and I'm going to be a petty ass bitch and give this fucking book two stars imsofuckingannoyedrightnowwhyisthishappeningughomgoooooodddddd<br /><br /><br />FUCK. skldmf ASDF BNKWEFHHSFDSJL J kjsfn kjadsfh2341284uO<br /><br /><b>2 FUCJING CONFUSING AND DIS<i>ASSS</i>POINTING STARS</b><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/branbookaddict" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/brandonthebookaddict/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookstagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/brandonthebookaddict" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> |</span>

<div id="review_2566122097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566122097" />
    <a title="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader"><img alt="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594344467p2/70951605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566122097?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

  <span id="freeText13965932188200503489" style="display:none"><b>[Edit: 8/30/2019]</b> - OMG, it has an <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt8244244/" rel="nofollow noopener">IMDB Page</a>!!<br>****************<br>One of my favorite books is going to be a <a href="https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/columbia-divergent-producers-tackling-ya-fantasy-hazel-wood-1011099" rel="nofollow noopener">movie</a>...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475082067ra/20679219.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>****************<br>I'm very glad my slump made me not read this in the summer this saving it for October so I could listen to the audiobook. (Which was narrated by my favorite narrator Rebecca Soler!!). <br><br>Anyway, this is a really unique book. It's kind of a fairy tale retelling except it's not actually retelling any tales. So I guess it's not a retelling. Basically, Alice what-her-last-name and her Mom are on the run from their bad luck. But soon Alice starts seeing characters from her Grandmother's mysterious fairy tale book. So basically it's like a dark version of Land of Stories. Soon enough Alice's mom disappears So Alice enlists the help of... Of Shaun? Seamus? I honestly don't remember his name hold on....<br>*Googles *<br>Nope I can't find anything.... I'm just gonna call him Shaun.. So Alice Proserpine! That's her name! Anyway, Alice enlists the help of Shaun to figure out what is going on and where her mother went.<br><br>The travel all over the place to dig up clues and try to figure out where to go and who to find. At the end, there is a major plot twist and it was amamzing!! In the end, I love this whole novel. <div id="review_2184168710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2184168710" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2184168710?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35121240-the-hazel-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=faerie">faerie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184168710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9684829710085554021">Review first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/the-hazel-wood/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>:<br/><br/>Alice Proserpine has always led a drifter’s life with her mother Ella. They scrape by on the edge of homelessness, constantly moving from place to place, staying with friends until they wear out their welcome, bad luck relentlessly dogging their footsteps wherever they go. And they never speak about Ella’s mother Althea, a reclusive author who lives in a grand, nearly impossible to find estate called the Hazel Wood, and who was famous for <i>Tales from the </i></span>
  <span id="freeText9684829710085554021" style="display:none">Review first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/the-hazel-wood/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>:<br /><br />Alice Proserpine has always led a drifter’s life with her mother Ella. They scrape by on the edge of homelessness, constantly moving from place to place, staying with friends until they wear out their welcome, bad luck relentlessly dogging their footsteps wherever they go. And they never speak about Ella’s mother Althea, a reclusive author who lives in a grand, nearly impossible to find estate called the Hazel Wood, and who was famous for <i>Tales from the Hinterland</i>, a mysterious, nearly impossible to find collection of dark and bloody fairy tales. All Alice knows about this tantalizing book (before her mother snatched it away from her, never to be seen again) is the titles of the stories, including the intriguingly named “Alice-Three-Times.”<br /><br />When Ella gets word that Althea has died, she’s determined to stop running from life. She marries a rich New Yorker after a whirlwind courtship and she and Alice try ― or not ― to adjust to a different lifestyle. Alice is seething with anger and frustration most of the time, and Ella’s marriage rapidly begins fraying.<br /><br />Then their lives get upended again, but in a way that blindsides Alice: Ella is kidnapped by two people who say they are from the Hinterland. She disappears without a trace, leaving behind only a message for Alice: “Stay the hell away from the Hazel Wood.” Which message, of course, Alice has absolutely no intention of heeding. Alice enlists her friend Ellery Finch, a longtime fan of <i>Tales from the Hinterland</i>, to help her in her search. But she has no idea where to find the Hazel Wood, or what awaits her there.<br /><br /><i>The Hazel Wood</i> begins as a quirky, bleak urban fantasy set in our contemporary world. In the first half of the book the plot unrolls at a leisurely pace, enlivened only by Ella’s kidnapping, Alice’s search for the Hazel Wood, and some occasional run-ins with suspicious dark characters. But the murky horror of the Hazel Wood and the Hinterland cast a gloom over every page, reinforced by Finch’s occasional retelling of some of the stories from the copy of <i>Tales of the Hinterland</i> that he read long ago.<br /><br />The pace picks up in the second half when the novel suddenly shifts gears to a dark fairy tale type of setting. I enjoyed the creativity and fantasy of this part of the novel much more than the first part, though I was underwhelmed at a couple of key points: the climactic scene and the ending both struck me as weak.<br /><br />Melissa Albert’s writing, though Alice’s first person narrative voice, was a major plus for me. Her language is lush and evocative, though I’ll admit it sometimes sidles toward purple prose:<blockquote>There was a funny glitter in [Ella’s] eyes as she watched herself in the mirror. I thought of that later, when she came home with a twin glitter on her ring finger: a rock as big as the Ritz.<br /><br />My memory of that night is tattered, a movie screen clawed to pieces. The glint of the ring lodged in my eye like a shard of demon glass, and the anger overwhelmed me.</blockquote>The main character, Alice, is rude, inconsiderate, foul-mouthed and, more often than not, angry; certainly not an easy character to appreciate. She's not at all politically correct, so readers sensitive to those nuances have an additional reasons to be perturbed with her point of view. Alice's main good point is her deep devotion and love for Ella. I wasn’t as irritated by her as Ray and Jana (my FanLit co-reviewers) were, partly because the reason for her irascible nature, when finally disclosed, was an unusual and compelling one. Still, the amount of swearing (a Kindle search informs me that there are 22 F-bombs in this book) was a definite turn-off for me for a YA fantasy.<br /><br />At one point Finch tells Alice:<blockquote>"I got my hands on Althea’s book. And it was perfect. There are no lessons in it. There’s just this harsh, horrible world touched with beautiful magic, where shitty things happen. And they don’t happen for a reason, or in threes, or in a way that looks like justice. They’re set in a place that has no rules and doesn’t want any."</blockquote>Much the same could be said of this book: It’s harsh and flawed but there’s creativity and beauty in it. Despite its shortcomings, I enjoyed <i>The Hazel Wood</i>.<br /><br />I received a free copy from the publisher through NetGalley for review. Thanks!<br /><br /><b>Original post:</b> Cheers! NetGalley just approved me for this YA fantasy, and I'm really excited about it! I was puttering around on NetGalley a few days ago and this book is at the very top of their "most requested" list. The first six chapters can be downloaded for free on Amazon, so I did. Melissa Albert's writing style pulled me right into the story, and I requested this book as soon as I finished reading those chapters. <br /><br />Now to find time to fit this into my overstuffed reading schedule ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9684829710085554021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2253479388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253479388" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253479388?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250192196" href="/book/show/36375387-the-hazel-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253479388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15683885795497111506">Seventeen-year-old Alice has never had reason to believe her grandmother's book of dark fairy tales is founded in truth - until now. When her mother is kidnapped by a mysterious figure who claims to be from the Hinterland – the dangerous supernatural world where her grandmother's stories are set – she must join forces with a classmate, Ellery Finch, whose cult-love of her grandmother's fairy tales are the key to finding the realm where her mother is being held captive. <br/><br/><i>The Hazel Wood</i> pays homage</span>
  <span id="freeText15683885795497111506" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Alice has never had reason to believe her grandmother's book of dark fairy tales is founded in truth - until now. When her mother is kidnapped by a mysterious figure who claims to be from the Hinterland – the dangerous supernatural world where her grandmother's stories are set – she must join forces with a classmate, Ellery Finch, whose cult-love of her grandmother's fairy tales are the key to finding the realm where her mother is being held captive. <br /><br /><i>The Hazel Wood</i> pays homage to fables and fairy tales by occasionally making light references to stories such as "The Three Little Pigs" when Alice questions, "<i>If you've spent your whole life running, how do you learn to stand still? How do you figure out the right way to turn your straw house into brick?</i>"* or "Hansel and Gretel" and "Rumpelstiltskin" when Althea Proserpine (Alice's grandmother) is asked by an interviewer how to get to her house in the Hazel Wood and she replies, "<i>You'd get lost on the way to finding me. You'd need breadcrumbs or a spool of thread.</i>"* <br /><br />Albert's prose flip-flops between lyrical and sensory to novice and bumbling. Some descriptions are liable to make readers swoon. "<i>Everything was echo and pulse, float and stretch, sleep and wake and a distant hunger</i>,"* Albert writes of Alice's experience waking after having been knocked out. "<i>A distant ray. I nipped at it like sugar water. Then a whoosh and a wrenching in my core, and the velvet dark ripped open.</i>"* When Alice watches Ellery open an old book, Albert drops readers into the scene by stating, "<i>a scent rose from its pages, the honey must of old print and something else - something sweet.</i>"* <br /><br />Albert's floral descriptions, however, are flattened by her irritating dependence on an awkward, redundant sentence structure employed to either regale readers with laughably bad similes or to spoon-feed her audience. For example: <br /><br /><i>Seeing it gave me a hot and cold feeling, like sweating in a winter coat.</i>*<br /><br /><i>The gun was drooping, like his arm was a dying stem.</i>*<br /><br /><i>She exhaled hard and spitty, like having to deal with me was too much to bear.</i>*<br /><br /><i>He bounced on the soles of his feet, like he was about to take off.</i>*<br /><br />Further shortcomings include a lackluster protagonist, a feeble attempt to touch on social issues, and a befuddling categorization in Young Adult literature when this book lacks the youthfulness of YA and more readily belongs with Adult Fiction. Perhaps publishers hoped to capitalize on Albert's professional career as the editor of the Barnes &amp; Noble Teen Blog? "She writes for teens, so her novel must be for teens," is a mathematical approach that doesn't quite compute in this situation. <br /><br /><i>The Hazel Wood</i> presents itself as a dark, foreboding tale but proves to be light reading. This over-hyped book with surface-level characters is neither creepy nor memorable. <br />- <br /><br />*Note: All quotes taken from an Advanced Reader Copy. <br /><br />Special thanks to <a href="https://us.macmillan.com/publishers/flatiron-books/" rel="nofollow noopener">Flatiron Books</a> for providing a free ARC of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15683885795497111506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5376236-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595863428p2/5376236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2219869192?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/5376236-heather">Heather</a>
